Species Description for nana:

Morphological Features:
Q: Q1: Is the general shape of the forewing broad or narrow, and is the forewing short or long compared to its width-to-length ratio?
A: The forewing is broad with a short width-to-length ratio.
Q: Q2: Is the general shape of the forewing oval, oblong oval, ovoid, or rhomboidal?
A: The general shape of the forewing is oblong oval.
Q: Q3: What is the color pattern of the entire forewing?
A: Forewing with pale brown veins and completely hyaline membrane.
Q: Q4: Is the entire forewing membrane densely covered in spinules, moderately, or sparsely?
A: The entire forewing membrane is moderately covered with spinules.
Q: Q5: Do spinules form a pattern? If so, is the pattern in transverse rows, hexagonal, two hexagonal rows, or randomly distributed?
A: The spinules form a pattern of two hexagonal rows.
Q: Q6: What color are the veins in the forewing?
A: The veins in the forewing are pale yellow.
Q: Q7: Is there color pigmentation present along the apices of the pterostigma and veins Rs, M1+2, M3+4, Cu1a, and Cu1b? If present, what are the colors?
A: No, there is no color pigmentation present along the apices of the pterostigma and veins Rs, M1+2, M3+4, Cu1a, and Cu1b.
Q: Q8: Are spinule-free strips present along the cell veins? If so, which ones, and are the spinule-free strips broad or narrow?
A: Spinule-free strips are present along all veins, and they are narrow.
Q: Q9: Is the shape of the apical two-thirds of vein C+Sc nearly straight, moderately convex, or strongly convex on the wing margin?
A: The shape of the apical two-thirds of vein C+Sc on the wing margin is nearly straight.
Q: Q10: Is vein C+Sc convex at base?
A: No, vein C+Sc is not convex at the base.
Q: Q11: Is there a costal break between vein C+Sc and the pterostigma if the pterostigma is present?
A: No, there is no costal break between vein C+Sc and the pterostigma if the pterostigma is present.
Q: Q12: Is the pterostigma cell present or absent?
A: Absent.
Q: Q13: If the pterostigma cell is present, is it as broad as it is long or short in length, and is it broad or narrow in relative width?
A: The pterostigma cell is present and is as broad as it is long.
Q: Q14: In which region of the pterostigma cell is it broadest; at the base or middle, or apical 2/3rds or apical 1/3rd?
A: The pterostigma cell is broadest at the apical 2/3.
Q: Q15: If the pterostigma cell is present, is the posterior vein of the pterostigma in the apical two-thirds relatively straight or moderately to broadly convex or is the posterior vein convex across its entire length?
A: The posterior vein of the pterostigma is moderately to broadly convex in the apical two-thirds.
Q: Q16: Vein Rs: Is it relatively straight or sinuate, and does it abruptly, moderately, or slightly turn up to the wing margin apically?
A: Vein Rs is relatively straight and slightly turns up to the wing margin apically.
Q: Q17: Is cell M1 relatively broad or narrow in width, and is it long or short in length compared to the total forewing length?
A: Cell M1 is relatively broad in width and short in length compared to the total forewing length.
Q: Q18: Vein Cu1a at the bottom of cell M2: Is it slightly, moderately, or strongly convex in the apical two-thirds or along the entire length of vein Cu1a?
A: Vein Cu1a at the bottom of cell M2 is strongly convex along its entire length.
Q: Q19: Is cell Cu1 broad or narrow in width, and is it short or long in length compared to the total forewing length?
A: Cell Cu1 is broad in width and long in length compared to the total forewing length.
Q: Q20: Is the apex of vein Cu1a strongly, moderately, or weakly arced towards the posterior margin of the forewing?
A: The apex of vein Cu1a is moderately arced towards the posterior margin of the forewing.
Q: Q21: Are the surface spinules absent or present on the basal one-third or one-half of cell C+Sc?
A: Surface spinules are absent on the basal one-half of cell C+Sc.
Q: Q22: In which part forewing is the widest: at base, or in the middle, or in apical two thirds, or in apical third?
A: The forewing is the widest in the middle.
Q: Q23: Is apical margin of forewing broadly rounded, or narrowly rounded, or triangular? If rounded, is apical margin evenly or unevenly rounded?
A: The apical margin of the forewing is broadly and evenly rounded.
Q: Q24: Is forewing membrane and/or veins covered by setae? If yes, are these setae long or short, densely or rarely distributed?
A: The forewing membrane and veins are without setae.

Species Description for adesmiae:

Morphological Features:
Q: Q1: Is the general shape of the forewing broad or narrow, and is the forewing short or long compared to its width-to-length ratio?
A: The forewing has a broad shape and is relatively short with a width-to-length ratio of 0.53–0.57.
Q: Q2: Is the general shape of the forewing oval, oblong oval, ovoid, or rhomboidal?
A: The general shape of the forewing is oblong oval.
Q: Q3: What is the color pattern of the entire forewing?
A: The entire forewing is pale brown with a distinct pattern of pale areas along the veins and in the middle of the cells.
Q: Q4: Is the entire forewing membrane densely covered in spinules, moderately, or sparsely?
A: The entire forewing membrane is densely covered with spinules.
Q: Q5: Do spinules form a pattern? If so, is the pattern in transverse rows, hexagonal, two hexagonal rows, or randomly distributed?
A: The spinules on the surface of the wing membrane form a pattern of transverse rows.
Q: Q6: What color are the veins in the forewing?
A: The veins in the forewing are pale brown.
Q: Q7: Is there color pigmentation present along the apices of the pterostigma and veins Rs, M1+2, M3+4, Cu1a, and Cu1b? If present, what are the colors?
A: Yes, there is color pigmentation present along the apices of the pterostigma and veins Rs, M1+2, M3+4, Cu1a, and Cu1b. The color is brown.
Q: Q8: Are spinule-free strips present along the cell veins? If so, which ones, and are the spinule-free strips broad or narrow?

Species Description for monticola:

Morphological Features:
Q: Q1: Is the general shape of the forewing broad or narrow, and is the forewing short or long compared to its width-to-length ratio?
A: The forewing is broad and short with a low width-to-length ratio.
Q: Q2: Is the general shape of the forewing oval, oblong oval, ovoid, or rhomboidal?
A: The general shape of the forewing is oblong oval.
Q: Q3: What is the color pattern of the entire forewing?
A: The entire forewing has a color pattern with a pale brown membrane and brown veins.
Q: Q4: Is the entire forewing membrane densely covered in spinules, moderately, or sparsely?
A: The entire forewing membrane is moderately covered with spinules.
Q: Q5: Do spinules form a pattern? If so, is the pattern in transverse rows, hexagonal, two hexagonal rows, or randomly distributed?
A: Spinules on the wing shown form a pattern of two hexagonal rows.
Q: Q6: What color are the veins in the forewing?
A: The veins in the forewing are yellowish-brown.
Q: Q7: Is there color pigmentation present along the apices of the pterostigma and veins Rs, M1+2, M3+4, Cu1a, and Cu1b? If present, what are the colors?
A: Yes, there is color pigmentation present along the apices of the pterostigma and veins Rs, M1+2, M3+4, Cu1a, and Cu1b. The color is brown.
Q: Q8: Are spinule-free strips present along the cell veins? If so, which ones, and are the spinule-free strips broad or narrow?
A: Yes, spinule-free strips are present along all the veins of the wing. These strips are narrow.
Q: Q9: Is the shape of the apical two-thirds of vein C+Sc nearly straight, moderately convex, or strongly convex on the wing margin?
A: The shape of the apical two-thirds of vein C+Sc on the wing margin is strongly convex.
Q: Q10: Is vein C+Sc convex at base?
A: No, the vein C+Sc is not convex at the base.
Q: Q11: Is there a costal break between vein C+Sc and the pterostigma if the pterostigma is present?
A: Yes, there is a costal break between vein C+Sc and the pterostigma if the pterostigma is present in the wing of *Dasineura trifolii*.
Q: Q12: Is the pterostigma cell present or absent?
A: Absent.
Q: Q13: If the pterostigma cell is present, is it as broad as it is long or short in length, and is it broad or narrow in relative width?
A: The pterostigma cell is present, short in length, and broad in relative width.
Q: Q14: In which region of the pterostigma cell is it broadest; at the base or middle, or apical 2/3rds or apical 1/3rd?
A: The pterostigma cell is broadest in the apical 2/3rds.
Q: Q15: If the pterostigma cell is present, is the posterior vein of the pterostigma in the apical two-thirds relatively straight or moderately to broadly convex or is the posterior vein convex across its entire length?
A: The posterior vein of the pterostigma is relatively straight in the apical two-thirds.
Q: Q16: Vein Rs: Is it relatively straight or sinuate, and does it abruptly, moderately, or slightly turn up to the wing margin apically?
A: Vein Rs is relatively straight and abruptly turns up to the wing margin apically.
Q: Q17: Is cell M1 relatively broad or narrow in width, and is it long or short in length compared to the total forewing length?
A: Cell M1 is relatively broad in width and short in length compared to the total forewing length.
Q: Q18: Vein Cu1a at the bottom of cell M2: Is it slightly, moderately, or strongly convex in the apical two-thirds or along the entire length of vein Cu1a?
A: Vein Cu1a at the bottom of cell M2 is strongly convex along the entire length.
Q: Q19: Is cell Cu1 broad or narrow in width, and is it short or long in length compared to the total forewing length?
A: Cell Cu1 is broad in width and long in length compared to the total forewing length.
Q: Q20: Is the apex of vein Cu1a strongly, moderately, or weakly arced towards the posterior margin of the forewing?
A: The apex of vein Cu1a is strongly arced towards the posterior margin of the forewing.
Q: Q21: Are the surface spinules absent or present on the basal one-third or one-half of cell C+Sc?
A: The surface spinules are absent on the basal one-third of cell C+Sc.
Q: Q22: In which part forewing is the widest: at base, or in the middle, or in apical two thirds, or in apical third?
A: The forewing is the widest in the middle.

A: The apical margin of the forewing is broadly and evenly rounded.

A: Forewing membrane and veins are without setae.

Species Description for longicauda:

Morphological Features:
Q: Q1: Is the general shape of the forewing broad or narrow, and is the forewing short or long compared to its width-to-length ratio?
A: The forewing has a broad shape and is relatively short with a high width-to-length ratio.
Q: Q2: Is the general shape of the forewing oval, oblong oval, ovoid, or rhomboidal?
A: The general shape of the forewing is oblong oval.
Q: Q3: What is the color pattern of the entire forewing?
A: The entire forewing is pale yellow with pale brown veins and distinct brown patches in the middle of the discal cell and at the base of the second subcostal, the first median and the cubital sectors.
Q: Q4: Is the entire forewing membrane densely covered in spinules, moderately, or sparsely?
A: The entire forewing membrane is sparsely covered with spinules.
Q: Q5: Do spinules form a pattern? If so, is the pattern in transverse rows, hexagonal, two hexagonal rows, or randomly distributed?
A: The spinules on the wing membrane of *Eutreta novaeboracensis* form a pattern of transverse rows.
Q: Q6: What color are the veins in the forewing?
A: The veins in the forewing are yellowish-brown.
Q: Q7: Is there color pigmentation present along the apices of the pterostigma and veins Rs, M1+2, M3+4, Cu1a, and Cu1b? If present, what are the colors?
A: No, there is no color pigmentation present along the apices of the pterostigma and veins Rs, M1+2, M3+4, Cu1a, and Cu1b.
Q: Q8: Are spinule-free strips present along the cell veins? If so, which ones, and are the spinule-free strips broad or narrow?
A: Spinule-free strips are present along all veins of the wing. These strips are narrow.
Q: Q9: Is the shape of the apical two-thirds of vein C+Sc nearly straight, moderately convex, or strongly convex on the wing margin?
A: The shape of the apical two-thirds of vein C+Sc on the wing margin is nearly straight.
Q: Q10: Is vein C+Sc convex at base?
A: Yes, the vein C+Sc is convex at the base.
Q: Q11: Is there a costal break between vein C+Sc and the pterostigma if the pterostigma is present?
A: No, there is no costal break between vein C+Sc and the pterostigma if the pterostigma is present.
Q: Q12: Is the pterostigma cell present or absent?
A: Absent.
Q: Q13: If the pterostigma cell is present, is it as broad as it is long or short in length, and is it broad or narrow in relative width?
A: The pterostigma cell is present, short in length, and broad in relative width.
Q: Q14: In which region of the pterostigma cell is it broadest; at the base or middle, or apical 2/3rds or apical 1/3rd?
A: The pterostigma is broadest in the apical 2/3.
Q: Q15: If the pterostigma cell is present, is the posterior vein of the pterostigma in the apical two-thirds relatively straight or moderately to broadly convex or is the posterior vein convex across its entire length?
A: The posterior vein of the pterostigma is convex across its entire length.
Q: Q16: Vein Rs: Is it relatively straight or sinuate, and does it abruptly, moderately, or slightly turn up to the wing margin apically?
A: Vein Rs is relatively straight and abruptly turns up to the wing margin apically.
Q: Q17: Is cell M1 relatively broad or narrow in width, and is it long or short in length compared to the total forewing length?
A: Cell M1 is relatively broad in width and short in length compared to the total forewing length.
Q: Q18: Vein Cu1a at the bottom of cell M2: Is it slightly, moderately, or strongly convex in the apical two-thirds or along the entire length of vein Cu1a?
A: Vein Cu1a at the bottom of cell M2 is strongly convex in the apical two-thirds.
Q: Q19: Is cell Cu1 broad or narrow in width, and is it short or long in length compared to the total forewing length?
A: Cell Cu1 is broad in width and long in length compared to the total forewing length.
Q: Q20: Is the apex of vein Cu1a strongly, moderately, or weakly arced towards the posterior margin of the forewing?
A: The apex of vein Cu1a is strongly arced towards the posterior margin of the forewing.
Q: Q21: Are the surface spinules absent or present on the basal one-third or one-half of cell C+Sc?
A: Surface spinules are absent on the basal half of cell C+Sc.
Q: Q22: In which part forewing is the widest: at base, or in the middle, or in apical two thirds, or in apical third?
A: The forewing is the widest in the middle.
Q: Q23: Is apical margin of forewing broadly rounded, or narrowly rounded, or triangular? If rounded, is apical margin evenly or unevenly rounded?
A: The apical margin of the forewing is broadly and evenly rounded.
Q: Q24: Is forewing membrane and/or veins covered by setae? If yes, are these setae long or short, densely or rarely distributed?
A: The forewing membrane is covered with short, densely distributed setae, while the veins are bare.

Species Description for chilensis:

Morphological Features:
Q: Q1: Is the general shape of the forewing broad or narrow, and is the forewing short or long compared to its width-to-length ratio?
A: The forewing has a broad shape and is relatively short, with a width-to-length ratio of approximately 0.5.
Q: Q2: Is the general shape of the forewing oval, oblong oval, ovoid, or rhomboidal?
A: The general shape of the forewing is oblong oval.
Q: Q3: What is the color pattern of the entire forewing?
A: The entire forewing is hyaline with pale brown veins and membrane.
Q: Q4: Is the entire forewing membrane densely covered in spinules, moderately, or sparsely?
A: The entire forewing membrane is moderately covered with spinules.
Q: Q5: Do spinules form a pattern? If so, is the pattern in transverse rows, hexagonal, two hexagonal rows, or randomly distributed?
A: The spinules on the wing membrane of *Aleurothrixus floccosus* form a pattern of two hexagonal rows.
Q: Q6: What color are the veins in the forewing?
A: The veins in the forewing are pale brown.
Q: Q7: Is there color pigmentation present along the apices of the pterostigma and veins Rs, M1+2, M3+4, Cu1a, and Cu1b? If present, what are the colors?
A: Yes, there is color pigmentation present along the apices of the pterostigma and veins Rs, M1+2, M3+4, Cu1a, and Cu1b. The color is brown.
Q: Q8: Are spinule-free strips present along the cell veins? If so, which ones, and are the spinule-free strips broad or narrow?
A: Yes, spinule-free strips are present along all veins of the wing. These strips are broad.
Q: Q9: Is the shape of the apical two-thirds of vein C+Sc nearly straight, moderately convex, or strongly convex on the wing margin?
A: The shape of the apical two-thirds of vein C+Sc on the wing margin is nearly straight.
Q: Q10: Is vein C+Sc convex at base?
A: No, the vein C+Sc is not convex at the base.
Q: Q11: Is there a costal break between vein C+Sc and the pterostigma if the pterostigma is present?
A: No, there is no costal break between vein C+Sc and the pterostigma if the pterostigma is present.
Q: Q12: Is the pterostigma cell present or absent?
A: The pterostigma cell is absent.
Q: Q13: If the pterostigma cell is present, is it as broad as it is long or short in length, and is it broad or narrow in relative width?
A: The pterostigma cell is present and is as broad as it is long, and relatively broad.
Q: Q14: In which region of the pterostigma cell is it broadest; at the base or middle, or apical 2/3rds or apical 1/3rd?
A: In the pterostigma cell of the wing shown, it is broadest in the apical 2/3rds.
Q: Q15: If the pterostigma cell is present, is the posterior vein of the pterostigma in the apical two-thirds relatively straight or moderately to broadly convex or is the posterior vein convex across its entire length?
A: The image shows a wing with a pterostigma cell present, and the posterior vein of the pterostigma is convex across its entire length.
Q: Q16: Vein Rs: Is it relatively straight or sinuate, and does it abruptly, moderately, or slightly turn up to the wing margin apically?
A: Vein Rs is relatively straight and slightly turns up to the wing margin apically.
Q: Q17: Is cell M1 relatively broad or narrow in width, and is it long or short in length compared to the total forewing length?
A: Cell M1 is relatively broad in width and short in length compared to the total forewing length.
Q: Q18: Vein Cu1a at the bottom of cell M2: Is it slightly, moderately, or strongly convex in the apical two-thirds or along the entire length of vein Cu1a?
A: Vein Cu1a at the bottom of cell M2 is strongly convex in the apical two-thirds.
Q: Q19: Is cell Cu1 broad or narrow in width, and is it short or long in length compared to the total forewing length?
A: Cell Cu1 is broad in width and long in length compared to the total forewing length.
Q: Q20: Is the apex of vein Cu1a strongly, moderately, or weakly arced towards the posterior margin of the forewing?
A: The apex of vein Cu1a is strongly arced towards the posterior margin of the forewing.
Q: Q21: Are the surface spinules absent or present on the basal one-third or one-half of cell C+Sc?
A: The surface spinules are absent on the basal one-third of cell C+Sc.
Q: Q22: In which part forewing is the widest: at base, or in the middle, or in apical two thirds, or in apical third?
A: The forewing is the widest in the apical third.
Q: Q23: Is apical margin of forewing broadly rounded, or narrowly rounded, or triangular? If rounded, is apical margin evenly or unevenly rounded?
A: The apical margin of the forewing is broadly and evenly rounded.
Q: Q24: Is forewing membrane and/or veins covered by setae? If yes, are these setae long or short, densely or rarely distributed?
A: Forewing membrane and veins are without setae.

Species Description for capsici:

Morphological Features:
Q: Q1: Is the general shape of the forewing broad or narrow, and is the forewing short or long compared to its width-to-length ratio?
A: The forewing has a broad shape and is short based on its width-to-length ratio.
Q: Q2: Is the general shape of the forewing oval, oblong oval, ovoid, or rhomboidal?
A: The general shape of the forewing is ovoid.
Q: Q3: What is the color pattern of the entire forewing?
A: The entire forewing has a distinct color pattern with a pale brownish band extending from the middle of the costa to the tornus, and a pale brownish area from the base of the costa to the middle of the wing, as well as scattered pale brown dots in the submedian area.
Q: Q4: Is the entire forewing membrane densely covered in spinules, moderately, or sparsely?
A: The entire forewing membrane is densely covered with spinules.
Q: Q5: Do spinules form a pattern? If so, is the pattern in transverse rows, hexagonal, two hexagonal rows, or randomly distributed?
A: The spinules form a pattern in two hexagonal rows.
Q: Q6: What color are the veins in the forewing?
A: The veins in the forewing are brown.
Q: Q7: Is there color pigmentation present along the apices of the pterostigma and veins Rs, M1+2, M3+4, Cu1a, and Cu1b? If present, what are the colors?
A: Yes, there is color pigmentation present along the apices of the pterostigma and veins Rs, M1+2, M3+4, Cu1a, and Cu1b. The color is dark brown.
Q: Q8: Are spinule-free strips present along the cell veins? If so, which ones, and are the spinule-free strips broad or narrow?
A: Yes, spinule-free strips are present along the cell veins dm and r4+5. These spinule-free strips are broad.
Q: Q9: Is the shape of the apical two-thirds of vein C+Sc nearly straight, moderately convex, or strongly convex on the wing margin?
A: The shape of the apical two-thirds of vein C+Sc on the wing margin is strongly convex.
Q: Q10: Is vein C+Sc convex at base?
A: Yes, vein C+Sc is convex at the base.
Q: Q11: Is there a costal break between vein C+Sc and the pterostigma if the pterostigma is present?
A: No, there is no costal break between vein C+Sc and the pterostigma if the pterostigma is present.
Q: Q12: Is the pterostigma cell present or absent?
A: Absent.
Q: Q13: If the pterostigma cell is present, is it as broad as it is long or short in length, and is it broad or narrow in relative width?
A: The pterostigma cell is present, short in length, and broad in relative width.
Q: Q14: In which region of the pterostigma cell is it broadest; at the base or middle, or apical 2/3rds or apical 1/3rd?
A: In the pterostigma cell of the given image, it is broadest in the apical 2/3.
Q: Q15: If the pterostigma cell is present, is the posterior vein of the pterostigma in the apical two-thirds relatively straight or moderately to broadly convex or is the posterior vein convex across its entire length?
A: The posterior vein of the pterostigma is relatively straight in the apical two-thirds.
Q: Q16: Vein Rs: Is it relatively straight or sinuate, and does it abruptly, moderately, or slightly turn up to the wing margin apically?
A: Vein Rs is relatively straight and abruptly turns up to the wing margin apically.
Q: Q17: Is cell M1 relatively broad or narrow in width, and is it long or short in length compared to the total forewing length?
A: Cell M1 is relatively broad in width and short in length compared to the total forewing length.
Q: Q18: Vein Cu1a at the bottom of cell M2: Is it slightly, moderately, or strongly convex in the apical two-thirds or along the entire length of vein Cu1a?
A: Vein Cu1a at the bottom of cell M2 is strongly convex in the apical two-thirds.
Q: Q19: Is cell Cu1 broad or narrow in width, and is it short or long in length compared to the total forewing length?
A: Cell Cu1 is broad in width and short in length compared to the total forewing length.
Q: Q20: Is the apex of vein Cu1a strongly, moderately, or weakly arced towards the posterior margin of the forewing?
A: The apex of vein Cu1a is strongly arced towards the posterior margin of the forewing.
Q: Q21: Are the surface spinules absent or present on the basal one-third or one-half of cell C+Sc?
A: The surface spinules are absent on the basal one-third of cell C+Sc.
Q: Q22: In which part forewing is the widest: at base, or in the middle, or in apical two thirds, or in apical third?
A: The forewing is widest in the middle.
Q: Q23: Is apical margin of forewing broadly rounded, or narrowly rounded, or triangular? If rounded, is apical margin evenly or unevenly rounded?
A: The apical margin of the forewing is broadly and unevenly rounded.
Q: Q24: Is forewing membrane and/or veins covered by setae? If yes, are these setae long or short, densely or rarely distributed?
A: Forewing membrane with short setae densely scattered along veins and sparsely between them.

Q: Q1: Is the general shape of the forewing broad or narrow, and is the forewing short or long compared to its width-to-length ratio?
A: The forewing has a broad shape and is short compared to its width-to-length ratio.
Q: Q2: Is the general shape of the forewing oval, oblong oval, ovoid, or rhomboidal?
A: The general shape of the forewing is oblong oval.
Q: Q3: What is the color pattern of the entire forewing?
A: The entire forewing is pale brown with dark brown dots scattered, more densely along veins, and with brownish smears in the middle of the wing and along the apical margin.
Q: Q4: Is the entire forewing membrane densely covered in spinules, moderately, or sparsely?
A: The entire forewing membrane is densely covered with spinules.
Q: Q5: Do spinules form a pattern? If so, is the pattern in transverse rows, hexagonal, two hexagonal rows, or randomly distributed?
A: The spinules form a pattern of two hexagonal rows.
Q: Q6: What color are the veins in the forewing?
A: The veins in the forewing are brown.
Q: Q7: Is there color pigmentation present along the apices of the pterostigma and veins Rs, M1+2, M3+4, Cu1a, and Cu1b? If present, what are the colors?
A: Yes, there is color pigmentation present along the apices of the pterostigma and veins Rs, M1+2, M3+4, Cu1a, and Cu1b. The color is dark brown.
Q: Q8: Are spinule-free strips present along the cell veins? If so, which ones, and are the spinule-free strips broad or narrow?
A: Yes, spinule-free strips are present along the veins of the forewing. They are narrow and present along all veins.
Q: Q9: Is the shape of the apical two-thirds of vein C+Sc nearly straight, moderately convex, or strongly convex on the wing margin?
A: The shape of the apical two-thirds of vein C+Sc on the wing margin is nearly straight.

A: No, the vein C+Sc is not convex at the base.
Q: Q11: Is there a costal break between vein C+Sc and the pterostigma if the pterostigma is present?
A: No, there is no costal break between vein C+Sc and the pterostigma if the pterostigma is present.
Q: Q12: Is the pterostigma cell present or absent?
A: Absent.
Q: Q13: If the pterostigma cell is present, is it as broad as it is long or short in length, and is it broad or narrow in relative width?
A: The pterostigma cell is present and is as broad as it is long, and broad in relative width.
Q: Q14: In which region of the pterostigma cell is it broadest; at the base or middle, or apical 2/3rds or apical 1/3rd?
A: The pterostigma cell is broadest at the apical 2/3.
Q: Q15: If the pterostigma cell is present, is the posterior vein of the pterostigma in the apical two-thirds relatively straight or moderately to broadly convex or is the posterior vein convex across its entire length?
A: The image shows a forewing with a pterostigma cell present, and the posterior vein of the pterostigma is convex across its entire length.
Q: Q16: Vein Rs: Is it relatively straight or sinuate, and does it abruptly, moderately, or slightly turn up to the wing margin apically?
A: Vein Rs is relatively straight and abruptly turns up to the wing margin apically.
Q: Q17: Is cell M1 relatively broad or narrow in width, and is it long or short in length compared to the total forewing length?
A: Cell M1 is relatively broad in width and short in length compared to the total forewing length.
Q: Q18: Vein Cu1a at the bottom of cell M2: Is it slightly, moderately, or strongly convex in the apical two-thirds or along the entire length of vein Cu1a?
A: Vein Cu1a at the bottom of cell M2 is strongly convex along its entire length.

A: Cell Cu1 is broad in width and short in length compared to the total forewing length.

A: The apex of vein Cu1a is strongly arced towards the posterior margin of the forewing.

A: Forewing membrane with dense, short setae, veins with relatively long setae.

Species Description for melaina:

Morphological Features:
Q: Q1: Is the general shape of the forewing broad or narrow, and is the forewing short or long compared to its width-to-length ratio?
A: The forewing is broad and long, with a width-to-length ratio of approximately 0.5.
Q: Q2: Is the general shape of the forewing oval, oblong oval, ovoid, or rhomboidal?
A: The general shape of the forewing is oblong oval.
Q: Q3: What is the color pattern of the entire forewing?
A: Forewing with pale brown veins and membrane.
Q: Q4: Is the entire forewing membrane densely covered in spinules, moderately, or sparsely?
A: The entire forewing membrane is sparsely covered with spinules.
Q: Q5: Do spinules form a pattern? If so, is the pattern in transverse rows, hexagonal, two hexagonal rows, or randomly distributed?
A: I don't know.
Q: Q6: What color are the veins in the forewing?
A: The veins in the forewing are pale yellow.
Q: Q7: Is there color pigmentation present along the apices of the pterostigma and veins Rs, M1+2, M3+4, Cu1a, and Cu1b? If present, what are the colors?
A: No, there is no color pigmentation present along the apices of the pterostigma and veins Rs, M1+2, M3+4, Cu1a, and Cu1b.
Q: Q8: Are spinule-free strips present along the cell veins? If so, which ones, and are the spinule-free strips broad or narrow?
A: Spinule-free strips are present along all veins in the image, and they are broad.
Q: Q9: Is the shape of the apical two-thirds of vein C+Sc nearly straight, moderately convex, or strongly convex on the wing margin?
A: The shape of the apical two-thirds of vein C+Sc on the wing margin is strongly convex.
Q: Q10: Is vein C+Sc convex at base?
A: Yes, the vein C+Sc is convex at the base.
Q: Q11: Is there a costal break between vein C+Sc and the pterostigma if the pterostigma is present?
A: No, there is no costal break between vein C+Sc and the pterostigma if the pterostigma is present.
Q: Q12: Is the pterostigma cell present or absent?
A: Absent.
Q: Q13: If the pterostigma cell is present, is it as broad as it is long or short in length, and is it broad or narrow in relative width?
A: The pterostigma cell is present and is as broad as it is long, and broad in relative width.
Q: Q14: In which region of the pterostigma cell is it broadest; at the base or middle, or apical 2/3rds or apical 1/3rd?
A: The pterostigma cell is broadest in the apical 2/3rds.
Q: Q15: If the pterostigma cell is present, is the posterior vein of the pterostigma in the apical two-thirds relatively straight or moderately to broadly convex or is the posterior vein convex across its entire length?
A: The posterior vein of the pterostigma is relatively straight in the apical two-thirds.
Q: Q16: Vein Rs: Is it relatively straight or sinuate, and does it abruptly, moderately, or slightly turn up to the wing margin apically?
A: Vein Rs is relatively straight and abruptly turns up to the wing margin apically.
Q: Q17: Is cell M1 relatively broad or narrow in width, and is it long or short in length compared to the total forewing length?
A: Cell M1 is relatively broad in width and short in length compared to the total forewing length.
Q: Q18: Vein Cu1a at the bottom of cell M2: Is it slightly, moderately, or strongly convex in the apical two-thirds or along the entire length of vein Cu1a?
A: Vein Cu1a at the bottom of cell M2 is strongly convex along its entire length.
Q: Q19: Is cell Cu1 broad or narrow in width, and is it short or long in length compared to the total forewing length?
A: Cell Cu1 is broad in width and short in length compared to the total forewing length.
Q: Q20: Is the apex of vein Cu1a strongly, moderately, or weakly arced towards the posterior margin of the forewing?
A: The apex of vein Cu1a is strongly arced towards the posterior margin of the forewing.
Q: Q21: Are the surface spinules absent or present on the basal one-third or one-half of cell C+Sc?
A: Surface spinules are absent on the basal one-half of cell C+Sc.
Q: Q22: In which part forewing is the widest: at base, or in the middle, or in apical two thirds, or in apical third?
A: The forewing is the widest in the middle.
Q: Q23: Is apical margin of forewing broadly rounded, or narrowly rounded, or triangular? If rounded, is apical margin evenly or unevenly rounded?
A: The apical margin of the forewing is broadly and evenly rounded.
Q: Q24: Is forewing membrane and/or veins covered by setae? If yes, are these setae long or short, densely or rarely distributed?
A: The forewing membrane and veins are without setae.

Morphological Features:
Q: Q1: Is the general shape of the forewing broad or narrow, and is the forewing short or long compared to its width-to-length ratio?
A: The forewing has a broad shape and is short compared to its width-to-length ratio.
Q: Q2: Is the general shape of the forewing oval, oblong oval, ovoid, or rhomboidal?
A: The general shape of the forewing is ovoid.
Q: Q3: What is the color pattern of the entire forewing?
A: The entire forewing has a pale yellowish-brown color pattern.
Q: Q4: Is the entire forewing membrane densely covered in spinules, moderately, or sparsely?
A: The entire forewing membrane is densely covered with spinules.
Q: Q5: Do spinules form a pattern? If so, is the pattern in transverse rows, hexagonal, two hexagonal rows, or randomly distributed?
A: The spinules on the wing form a pattern of two hexagonal rows.
Q: Q6: What color are the veins in the forewing?
A: The veins in the forewing are yellowish-brown.
Q: Q7: Is there color pigmentation present along the apices of the pterostigma and veins Rs, M1+2, M3+4, Cu1a, and Cu1b? If present, what are the colors?
A: No, there is no color pigmentation present along the apices of the pterostigma and veins Rs, M1+2, M3+4, Cu1a, and Cu1b.
Q: Q8: Are spinule-free strips present along the cell veins? If so, which ones, and are the spinule-free strips broad or narrow?
A: Spinule-free strips are present along all veins of the wing. These strips are narrow.
Q: Q9: Is the shape of the apical two-thirds of vein C+Sc nearly straight, moderately convex, or strongly convex on the wing margin?
A: The shape of the apical two-thirds of vein C+Sc on the wing margin is strongly convex.
Q: Q10: Is vein C+Sc convex at base?
A: No, vein C+Sc is not convex at the base.
Q: Q11: Is there a costal break between vein C+Sc and the pterostigma if the pterostigma is present?
A: No, there is no costal break between vein C+Sc and the pterostigma if the pterostigma is present.
Q: Q12: Is the pterostigma cell present or absent?
A: Absent.
Q: Q13: If the pterostigma cell is present, is it as broad as it is long or short in length, and is it broad or narrow in relative width?
A: The pterostigma cell is present and is as broad as it is long, and narrow in relative width.
Q: Q14: In which region of the pterostigma cell is it broadest; at the base or middle, or apical 2/3rds or apical 1/3rd?
A: The pterostigma is broadest at the apical 2/3.
Q: Q15: If the pterostigma cell is present, is the posterior vein of the pterostigma in the apical two-thirds relatively straight or moderately to broadly convex or is the posterior vein convex across its entire length?
A: The posterior vein of the pterostigma is convex across its entire length.
Q: Q16: Vein Rs: Is it relatively straight or sinuate, and does it abruptly, moderately, or slightly turn up to the wing margin apically?
A: Vein Rs is relatively straight and abruptly turns up to the wing margin apically.
Q: Q17: Is cell M1 relatively broad or narrow in width, and is it long or short in length compared to the total forewing length?
A: Cell M1 is relatively narrow in width and long in length compared to the total forewing length.
Q: Q18: Vein Cu1a at the bottom of cell M2: Is it slightly, moderately, or strongly convex in the apical two-thirds or along the entire length of vein Cu1a?
A: Vein Cu1a at the bottom of cell M2 is strongly convex along its entire length.
Q: Q19: Is cell Cu1 broad or narrow in width, and is it short or long in length compared to the total forewing length?
A: Cell Cu1 is broad in width and short in length compared to the total forewing length.
Q: Q20: Is the apex of vein Cu1a strongly, moderately, or weakly arced towards the posterior margin of the forewing?
A: The apex of vein Cu1a is strongly arced towards the posterior margin of the forewing.
Q: Q21: Are the surface spinules absent or present on the basal one-third or one-half of cell C+Sc?
A: Surface spinules are absent on the basal one-half of cell C+Sc.
Q: Q22: In which part forewing is the widest: at base, or in the middle, or in apical two thirds, or in apical third?
A: The forewing is widest in the middle.

A: The apical margin of the forewing is broadly and unevenly rounded.

A: The forewing membrane is covered with short setae, which are densely distributed, and the veins are covered with long, dense setae.

Morphological Features:
Q: Q1: Is the general shape of the forewing broad or narrow, and is the forewing short or long compared to its width-to-length ratio?
A: The forewing has a broad shape and is short compared to its width-to-length ratio.
Q: Q2: Is the general shape of the forewing oval, oblong oval, ovoid, or rhomboidal?
A: The general shape of the forewing is oblong oval.
Q: Q3: What is the color pattern of the entire forewing?
A: The entire forewing has a color pattern with brown veins and a brownish-yellow membrane, with distinct brown pattern consisting of large spot in the middle of the costal margin, large median band stretching from the base of the 2nd radial cell to the apical part of the Cu1 cell, and large spot in the apical part of the wing.
Q: Q4: Is the entire forewing membrane densely covered in spinules, moderately, or sparsely?
A: The entire forewing membrane is moderately covered with spinules.

A: The spinules on the wing membrane of *Drosophila suzukii* do not form a distinct pattern.

A: The veins in the forewing are brown.

Q: Q8: Are spinule-free strips present along the cell veins? If so, which ones, and are the spinule-free strips broad or narrow?
A: Yes, spinule-free strips are present along all veins. These strips are narrow.

A: The shape of the apical two-thirds of vein C+Sc on the wing margin is nearly straight.

A: No, the vein C+Sc is not convex at the base.
Q: Q11: Is there a costal break between vein C+Sc and the pterostigma if the pterostigma is present?
A: No, there is no costal break between vein C+Sc and the pterostigma.
Q: Q12: Is the pterostigma cell present or absent?
A: Absent.

A: The pterostigma is broadest at the apical 2/3.

A: If the pterostigma cell is present, the posterior vein of the pterostigma in the apical two-thirds is relatively straight.
Q: Q16: Vein Rs: Is it relatively straight or sinuate, and does it abruptly, moderately, or slightly turn up to the wing margin apically?
A: Vein Rs is slightly sinuate and abruptly turns up to the wing margin apically.

A: Cell M1 is relatively broad in width and short in length compared to the total forewing length.

A: Cell Cu1 is broad and short compared to the total forewing length.

A: The apex of vein Cu1a is strongly arced towards the posterior margin of the forewing.

A: Surface spinules are absent on the basal one-third of cell C+Sc.

A: The forewing is the widest in the middle.

A: The apex of vein Cu1a is strongly arced towards the posterior margin of the forewing.

A: Surface spinules are absent on the basal one-half of cell C+Sc.

A: The forewing is widest in the middle.

A: The apical margin of the forewing is broadly and evenly rounded.
Q: Q24: Is forewing membrane and/or veins covered by setae? If yes, are these setae long or short, densely or rarely distributed?
A: Forewing membrane and veins are without setae.

Species Description for setosa:

Morphological Features:
Q: Q1: Is the general shape of the forewing broad or narrow, and is the forewing short or long compared to its width-to-length ratio?
A: The forewing is broad and short with a low width-to-length ratio.
Q: Q2: Is the general shape of the forewing oval, oblong oval, ovoid, or rhomboidal?
A: The general shape of the forewing is oblong oval.
Q: Q3: What is the color pattern of the entire forewing?
A: The entire forewing has a pale yellow to brown color pattern with veins that are concolorous with the membrane and distinct brown dots scattered all over the wing.
Q: Q4: Is the entire forewing membrane densely covered in spinules, moderately, or sparsely?
A: The entire forewing membrane is densely covered with spinules.
Q: Q5: Do spinules form a pattern? If so, is the pattern in transverse rows, hexagonal, two hexagonal rows, or randomly distributed?
A: Spinules on the wing shown form a pattern of two hexagonal rows.
Q: Q6: What color are the veins in the forewing?
A: The veins in the forewing are pale yellow.
Q: Q7: Is there color pigmentation present along the apices of the pterostigma and veins Rs, M1+2, M3+4, Cu1a, and Cu1b? If present, what are the colors?
A: There is no color pigmentation present along the apices of the pterostigma and veins Rs, M1+2, M3+4, Cu1a, and Cu1b.
Q: Q8: Are spinule-free strips present along the cell veins? If so, which ones, and are the spinule-free strips broad or narrow?
A: Spinule-free strips are present along all veins of the wing, and they are narrow.
Q: Q9: Is the shape of the apical two-thirds of vein C+Sc nearly straight, moderately convex, or strongly convex on the wing margin?
A: The shape of the apical two-thirds of vein C+Sc on the wing margin is moderately convex.
Q: Q10: Is vein C+Sc convex at base?
A: No, vein C+Sc is not convex at the base.
Q: Q11: Is there a costal break between vein C+Sc and the pterostigma if the pterostigma is present?
A: No, there is no costal break between vein C+Sc and the pterostigma if the pterostigma is present.
Q: Q12: Is the pterostigma cell present or absent?
A: The pterostigma cell is absent.
Q: Q13: If the pterostigma cell is present, is it as broad as it is long or short in length, and is it broad or narrow in relative width?
A: The pterostigma cell is present, short in length, and broad in relative width.
Q: Q14: In which region of the pterostigma cell is it broadest; at the base or middle, or apical 2/3rds or apical 1/3rd?
A: The pterostigma is broadest at the apical 2/3.
Q: Q15: If the pterostigma cell is present, is the posterior vein of the pterostigma in the apical two-thirds relatively straight or moderately to broadly convex or is the posterior vein convex across its entire length?
A: The posterior vein of the pterostigma in the apical two-thirds is relatively straight.
Q: Q16: Vein Rs: Is it relatively straight or sinuate, and does it abruptly, moderately, or slightly turn up to the wing margin apically?
A: Vein Rs is relatively straight and abruptly turns up to the wing margin apically.

A: Cell M1 is relatively broad in width and short in length compared to the total forewing length.

A: Vein Cu1a at the bottom of cell M2 is strongly convex along its entire length.
Q: Q19: Is cell Cu1 broad or narrow in width, and is it short or long in length compared to the total forewing length?
A: Cell Cu1 is broad in width and long in length compared to the total forewing length.

A: The apex of vein Cu1a is strongly arced towards the posterior margin of the forewing.

A: Surface spinules are absent on the basal one-half of cell C+Sc.
